Current Commentary

Prospects for the Second Internal Affairs Conference 20

The Kuomintang's Third Plenary Session is scheduled to convene on the 15th. With over forty members having decided to attend, surpassing the quorum of thirty-seven, the assembly is unlikely to fail. It is rumored that the conference will primarily discuss foreign affairs and domestic policies. At this critical juncture of national crisis, while a diplomatic strategy must be determined, domestic reform is also urgently needed. Moreover, these two aspects are closely interconnected. Now, prior to the Third Plenary Session, the Second Internal Affairs Conference, which commenced yesterday and witnessed enthusiastic attendance, further underscores the central government's special emphasis on internal affairs. Their intent to proceed with orderly steps towards genuine remedies sets them apart from the empty formalities and ineffectual approaches of the past. The Kuomintang is currently the sole political party wielding governing power in our nation, and the Ministry of Internal Affairs is the most crucial agency for implementing all national policies. When holding significant meetings, no one detached from politics can fail to harbor earnest expectations and sympathy. However, considering past conferences, proposals were invariably grand, and speeches invariably impassioned, yet resolutions were often shelved indefinitely. The fervent atmosphere would dissipate as the conference concluded, rendering the assembly meaningless. Its value was equivalent to a casual chat among gentlemen, a mere pastime. After repeated disappointments, outsiders can hardly be blamed for their indifference. Prior to this Internal Affairs Conference, key figures informally expressed their views, recognizing the futility of empty rhetoric and emphasizing the necessity of practical implementation. There should be a transformation, signifying a fresh start for this session. As the ancients said, "Effective governance lies not in verbose pronouncements." I urge all representatives attending the conference to deeply contemplate and savor these words.

In reforming domestic affairs, the first priority is to rectify officialdom. Achieving this involves various approaches. Regarding the current malpractices, the following three principles merit attention:

Firstly, clearly define responsibilities. Most middle and lower-level administrative officials today are ignorant of the true meaning of governance. They lack ambition before taking office and have no strategies after assuming their posts. Their goal is to enrich themselves at the expense of the nation, employing cunning and evasiveness as means. The better ones seek only to avoid mistakes, while the worse ones inflict suffering on the populace. Under the illusion of stability, they procrastinate. When faced with pressure, they abruptly resign. Thus, in terms of construction, it is like climbing a tree to catch fish; in terms of serving the people, it is akin to trying to satisfy hunger with pictures of cakes. What "governance" can be expected from such "officials?" The remedy lies in rigorously establishing regulations, assigning responsibilities, and conducting thorough assessments, with clear rewards and punishments. Crucially, they must not be allowed to simply walk away. Officials must realize that their positions are not trivial sinecures, and their departures cannot be easily arranged. Only then can we prevent corruption and block the path of opportunists.

Secondly, strictly stipulate penalties. The rampant corruption among politicians today is an undeniable fact. This corruption stems from the lack of self-respect among deceitful individuals who readily break the law. However, it also results from the leniency of the law, which fails to deter potential offenders. Those who arrive empty-handed leave with overflowing coffers, aiming to amass wealth rather than retain their official posts. Removal from office or dismissal holds little consequence. Demerits and salary deductions are even less concerning. Therefore, the severity of penalties in anti-corruption laws must be increased. Furthermore, a targeted approach is crucial, starting with confiscation of assets, followed by the most severe punishments. This may deter corruption and eliminate favoritism.

Thirdly, ensure reliable guarantees. Among those in government service, are there no upright individuals besides the corrupt and cunning? However, lacking job security, they cannot fully implement their plans. They may be transferred shortly after taking office, or their policies may be abruptly halted. Disheartened, they may resort to procrastination and extortion. It is said that a certain bureau chief, upon taking office, was presented with a meticulously crafted financial plan by his advisors. The bureau chief smiled and said, "The plan is undeniably thorough, but its effectiveness will only be seen after ten years at the earliest. This position will likely change hands multiple times by then." This sentiment is shared by many capable individuals and is the crux of preventing a clean and bright political landscape. Therefore, this Internal Affairs Conference should establish a method for guaranteeing tenure, ensuring that the appointment of lower-level officials is not subject to the whims of superiors. Furthermore, career civil servants should not be transferred along with political appointees. Through the passage of time, a harmonious relationship can be fostered between officials and the people, which would have a positive impact on future cooperation. This is different from those with a "five-day mayor" mentality. Although what has been said above are platitudes, they represent the common aspirations of the people. I dare to take advantage of this opportunity to reiterate them, in order to urge the authorities to pay attention and implement them earnestly.

Huang Shaoxiong

Inspecting the Capital Police 22

Inviting Members of the Internal Affairs Conference to Observe

Huang Personally Bestowed the "Governance and National Protection" Banner

Nanjing, Minister of Internal Affairs Huang Shaoxiong inspected the capital police at the Central Military Academy parade ground in the capital on the morning of the 10th, inviting all members of the Internal Affairs Conference to observe. Director Wu Siyu and Chief Inspector Li Jinde served as commanders. Minister Huang, along with Vice Ministers Gan Naiguang and Luo Gonghua, arrived at the parade ground around 9 a.m. The inspection commenced at 9:30 a.m. Guests included Peng Xuepei, Shu Ren, Wang Yongbin, and approximately several hundred members of the Internal Affairs Conference. Huang Shaoxiong, wearing a five-star police uniform, rode on horseback with Vice Ministers Gan Naiguang and Luo Gonghua, Police Administration Director Li Songfeng, and Wang Hao et al., to inspect each unit. The units inspected were the security team, special service team, training institute, police officers from various bureaus, female police team, police car team, mounted team, bicycle team, and motorcycle team, all under the jurisdiction of the Capital Police Department.

Minister of Internal Affairs Inspects the Capital Police (Photograph by Guanghua, Nanjing) 23

The order of the units was as follows: (1) Flag guard, (2) Band, (3) First Battalion, (4) Second Battalion, (5) Third Battalion, (6) Fourth Battalion, (7) Mounted team, (8) Bicycle team, (9) Motorcycle team, (10) Police vehicle team. Following the review of the units, skills were reviewed, including drills, martial arts, and Tai Chi by the female police. Then, the Minister delivered a speech, stating that this Internal Affairs Conference intends to draw the attention of the nation to police reform, providing an opportunity for representatives from various provinces to observe, in order to serve as a reference for police reform upon their return to their respective provinces. Furthermore, it is to allow the capital police force to recognize its position in the nation's police system. Subsequently, Minister Huang personally presented the "Governance and National Protection" banner to Director Wu. The ceremony concluded at 11 a.m. At noon, Wu Siyu hosted a luncheon at the Zhi Zhi Society. (Central News Agency Dispatch, 11th)

Internal Affairs Conference

Members Visited the Mausoleum Yesterday 24

Held Group Discussions to Review Proposals

Nanjing, All members of the Internal Affairs Conference visited the Sun Yat-sen Mausoleum at 2 p.m. on the 11th, with Minister Huang presiding. Approximately over one hundred people attended, including Luo Gonghua and all members. The order of the mausoleum visit ceremony was as follows: (1) All stood at attention, (2) Music played, (3) Party anthem sung, (4) Three bows performed before the portrait of the Premier, (5) The chairman presented a wreath, (6) Silent adjustment of clothing in the chamber, (7) Returned to position and bowed three times, (8) Music played, (9) Ceremony concluded. After the mausoleum visit, the members returned to the Internal Affairs Conference venue and held group discussions to review the proposals. (Central News Agency Dispatch, 11th)

Nanjing, Chiang proposed to the Internal Affairs Conference the re-enactment of local self-government regulations for counties and districts, and the implementation of Baojia below districts or towns, etc., with four attached measures. The ordinance on establishing Baojia household registration in counties within communist suppression areas, forty articles. Chiang also proposed amendments to the organization of local administrative agencies, with attached amendments to Article 5 of the provincial government organization law, three suggestions for amending the county organization law, two suggestions for dividing administrative regions, the organizational regulations of the administrative inspectorates in the communist suppression areas, twenty-three articles, and the organizational regulations of the county offices in the communist suppression areas, eighteen articles, pending the general assembly's resolution. (Special Dispatch, 11th)

Nanchang, The Jiangxi Provincial Government will submit a report and proposals to the Internal Affairs Conference today, transported by plane to Nanjing. (Special Dispatch, 11th)

Fellow Provincials from Guizhou Residing in Nanjing

Called an Emergency Meeting 25

Petitioning the Central Government···

To Stop the Civil War in Guizhou

Nanjing, Fellow Guizhou provincials residing in Nanjing held an emergency meeting and resolved: (1) To petition the central government to swiftly adopt effective measures to stop the civil war in Guizhou. (2) To petition the central government to thoroughly reform Guizhou's administration, appointing advanced party and national figures, regardless of regional origin, to serve as chairman of Guizhou, in order to prevent disputes. (3) To send a telegram in the name of the general assembly to Mao Guangxiang, urging both sides to quickly cease hostilities and await resolution by the central government. (6) To telegraph the people of Guizhou to resist excessive taxation and not support warlords. (Special Dispatch, 11th)

Zhangjia and His Entourage Arrive in Nanjing

Nanjing, Zhangjia arrived at Pukou at 1:00 p.m. on the 11th via special train, then crossed the Yangtze River and took a car to Lizi Society for a brief rest. Those who crossed the river to welcome him at Pukou included Central Committee members Bai Yunti, Zhao Bulian, and Keerke et al., totaling several dozen people. Zhangjia was born in the 21st year before the founding of the Republic of China and is currently 41 years old. The reporter visited his residence at noon and had the honor of hearing his statement, which roughly stated that since receiving the appointment as Propagation Envoy, he has long desired to visit Nanjing. Five Major Powers Disarmament

The Conference Takes a Sharp Turn 42

Five Countries Issue a Compromise Declaration 43

Germany Will Re-Enter the Disarmament Conference 44

▲Reuters, Geneva, 10th: If everything goes smoothly and there are no unexpected twists and turns, Germany will be able to re-enter the Disarmament Conference soon. The draft plan regarding this matter, which is satisfactory to the representatives of France and Germany, has been finalized tonight. A press release stated that the representatives of the five major powers talked all day, and at 7:30 p.m., they agreed on a method for the governments of France, Germany, and Italy to negotiate on their own. During the negotiations, French representative Paul-Boncour left the conference room three times to make phone calls to Paris to consult with Herriot. When Paul-Boncour hurriedly returned to his hotel, he told a Reuters reporter that things were not going badly, but were not yet finalized. German Foreign Minister Neurath originally planned to return to Berlin tomorrow morning, but has postponed his trip until later in the evening. The hope of the negotiations can be seen from this. British Prime Minister MacDonald is scheduled to have dinner with Paul-Boncour, Neurath, and American representative Davis tomorrow night before departing for London.

▲Reuters, Geneva, 11th: Representatives of the five major powers have signed a declaration stating that the governments of Britain, France, and Italy have announced the principles guiding the Disarmament Conference, one of which is to allow Germany (which must disarm according to the treaty) to enjoy equality in rights and methods. The Disarmament Conference will discuss the implementation of this principle in the future. The governments of Britain, France, Italy, and Germany jointly make a solemn statement that European countries rely on military force. The U.S. government and the governments of the other four countries have decided to cooperate in the conference to seek real methods to reduce and limit armaments.

▲Reuters, Geneva, 11th: Germany has accepted the arms equality plan. The German representative is expected to participate in the meeting of the main committee of the Disarmament Conference on December 13 and participate in the meeting of the General Committee on the 14th.

▲The National News Agency, Geneva, 11th: The compromise declaration agreed upon at the Five-Power Conference was signed this afternoon at the Hotel Beau-Rivage, where British Prime Minister MacDonald was staying. US Ambassador Davis, British Foreign Minister Simon, French Minister of War Paul-Boncour, German Foreign Minister Neurath, and Italian representative Aloisi all signed it. After the signing, MacDonald, Neurath, and Paul-Boncour will return to their respective countries tonight.

Solution to Equality Demands 45

▲Reuters, Geneva, 10th: Today's news is that there is now a resolution to the demand for equal status. British Prime Minister MacDonald congratulated this at a dinner party. The French government has agreed to this plan, and the German government will also have a satisfactory reply. If the governments of Britain, Italy, and the United States agree, there will be no doubt. It is reported that this plan stipulates: (1) According to the policy suspected by Herriot, it declares the equality of the status of Germany and other disarmed countries, but states that the method of realizing equality must be planned together with the security issue at the Disarmament Conference. (2) Britain, France, Italy, and the United States (excluding the United States) issue a declaration based on the declaration drafted by British Foreign Minister Simon, declaring that they will not use force as an instrument of national policy. Other countries can also issue the same declaration. (3) British Prime Minister MacDonald will notify the chairman of the Disarmament Conference, telling him that Germany will resume participating in the discussions of the conference.

Japanese Disarmament Proposal

Seizing Pacific Hegemony 46

Great Shock in All Sectors of Britain 47

▲Reuters, Paris, 11th: Le Temps said that Japan's naval proposals have caused great shock in all sectors of Britain because Japan mentioned the London Treaty and the Washington Treaty, which was unexpected. The newspaper said that Japan's proposal is particularly favorable to France, because it has made concessions to France on the number of effective units. It also retains the convenience of compromising with Italy. Le Peuple said that the figures put forward by Japan actually guarantee its hegemony in the Pacific.

▲Reuters, Tokyo, 11th: Japan's disarmament proposal to the five major powers was officially released today, with a seven-page explanatory memorandum detailing the principles on which maritime disarmament should be based. The main points are that the current scope of the Disarmament Conference is too large, making it difficult to establish a satisfactory and implementable maritime disarmament agreement, and that the new ratio of capital ships should be 11 for Britain and the United States respectively, and 8 for Japan, to replace the ratio of 5:5:3 stipulated in the 1930 London Naval Treaty. Japan's current proposed proposal is: (1) The tonnage and caliber of various warships should be as follows:

Tonnage Caliber (inches)

Capital Ships 25,000 14

First-Class Cruisers 8,000 8

Second-Class Cruisers 6,000 6.1

Destroyers 1,500 5.1

Submarines 1,800 5.1

As for aircraft carriers, they should be completely abolished, and warships should not be allowed to have equipment for the take-off and landing of seaplanes. (2) The maximum number of capital ships should be 11 each for Britain and the United States, 8 for Japan, 12 each for first-class cruisers for Britain and the United States, and 7 each for France and Italy. (3) The maximum tonnage of second-class cruisers in the five countries should be set at 150,000 tons each, and the same for destroyers. Submarines should have a maximum tonnage of 75,000 tons. The principles that Japan intends to reduce its navy on are to reduce offensive power and increase defensive power. Therefore, it advocates reducing the tonnage of various warships, such as capital ships and first-class cruisers, and dividing naval power into powerful types that emphasize relative strength and lighter types for patrolling coasts and sea routes, and for defense. The tonnage and nature of the latter category are determined by the local situation. Japan proposes to divide the world into the Pacific Group, the Atlantic Group, the European Group, and the South American Group, and then determine the quantitative limitations on armaments based on this. Japan advocates that a general agreement on general events should be negotiated first, and then special agreements on local issues and other issues should be formulated.

Present Situation of the Volunteer Army in Heilongjiang 48

Special dispatch from Harbin: The two provinces of Liaoning and Jilin have already been occupied by Japan. Heilongjiang and northern Jilin have also fallen one after another due to being isolated and without assistance. Although General Ma Zhanshan once used the extremely painful strategy of self-inflicted injury to try to connect with various units, hoping to overthrow the puppet state of Manchukuo in one fell swoop, it would still be a stroke of luck amid misfortune. However, after the second uprising, even if all the flesh and blood, and the sincerity of patriotism, were sacrificed, it could only leave a page of painful history filled with bloodstains in the history of national struggle for future generations to strive for. After General Ma encountered a glorious failure, the wealthy people of the Northeast could only sob in despair, and the hard-working farmers could only wait to be exploited and slaughtered by imperialism. However, under the command of the puppet state, not everyone is a puppet. There are those who pretend to be puppets, shocking national heroes. Who is this person? It is Su Bingwen, the Commander-in-Chief of the Northeast National Salvation Army.

Under the rule of the puppet state of Manchukuo, although officers of various units reluctantly accepted the appointment of the puppet state, they initially thought that negotiations with Japan were only a matter of time, and that the original state of the Republic of China would eventually be restored. However, as the situation dragged on, it seemed impossible to reverse the situation. Ordinary people were very disappointed, and even officers with a little conscience were filled with resentment. Patriots were all furious. Commander Su Bingwen's preparations for rebellion were not yet sufficient, but the various units of the Volunteer Army in northern Manchuria had run out of ammunition and food. If no reinforcements joined, all previous efforts would be in vain. Therefore, Commander Su could not wait for the time to be ripe or for preparations to be sufficient and resolutely launched the uprising. On the day of the uprising (September 27), he summoned Yamazaki, the Japanese Consul in Manzhouli, Uno, the Chief of the Police Force, and Kohara, the Chief of the Special Service Organ, to the Manzhouli Military Command Headquarters to talk. He immediately ordered them to instruct the garrison to disarm, while women and children could be released and allowed to leave the country. Japanese and puppet officials would be temporarily detained here. Upon hearing of the rebellion of the Chinese army, the garrison disarmed after negotiations. Although Uno was tyrannical and did evil, it was limited, while Kohara was imprisoned for specializing in extortion. Thus, the evil forces were eradicated, our rivers and mountains were restored, and the flag of the Blue Sky with a White Sun was seen again. Social order was exceptionally peaceful, and the people were happy, celebrating the relief of their suffering.

After Su Bingwen launched the uprising in Manzhouli, Zhang Dianjiu, Xie Ke, Jin Kuibi, Pu Bingshan, and 41 others sent a telegram on September 30, supporting Su as the Commander-in-Chief of the Northeast People's National Salvation Army and placing all their troops under his command. On October 1, Su Bingwen established the Heilongjiang Provincial Government in Manzhouli, telegraphed the whole country, and took office as the Commander-in-Chief of the National Salvation Army, vowing to resist Japan. Zhang Dianjiu was the Deputy Commander, Xie Ke was the Chief of Staff, and Jin Biku was the Deputy Chief of Staff. The telegram stated: "Our 30 million people in the Northeast have been brutally trampled under the iron hooves of the invaders. We cannot seek death, and we cannot survive. We have been in dire straits for more than a year... But the people's hearts have not died, and the country cannot be destroyed. How can we allow snoring next to our beds? I, Wen, have been waiting on the border, and have been dealing with the national crisis with great care. Fortunately, an inch of land has been preserved. Now, I have been entrusted by the people and supported by the generals, leading the volunteer army to fight for justice and sacrifice myself to serve the country without fear of sacrifice... I must make the true feelings of our 30 million people in the Northeast clear to the world, eliminate the puppet state, eradicate the traitors, expose the tricks of the brutal bandits, and restore the inherent land of China. With the destruction of our homes and the loss of our country, we have long made up our minds to sacrifice ourselves. Even if our strength is exhausted, we must wash away the shame of Li Ling..." The telegram listed the Japanese's atrocities against us and the various conspiracies to create the puppet state. It was a tragic and inspiring act, the most inspiring for the people of the Northeast to resist the strong since Ma Zhanshan's anti-Japanese uprising. Su himself only had two infantry brigades, eight independent companies, and one technical battalion, stationed from Luobin in the east to Boketu. At this time, the people's militia and volunteer army in various counties totaled about 50,000 people. Li Haiqing's troops and Ma Zhanshan in eastern Heilongjiang echoed each other and prepared to jointly attack Heihe. Su's troops, led by Wu Yushu, with more than 2,000 men, crossed the river from the lower reaches of the Nen River on the first day and began to attack Ang'angxi. Zhang Dianjiu's first brigade was responsible for the front of the Middle East Road, approaching Bu Kui directly from the Nen River Bridge. Li Haiqing's troops, with 5,000 men, and Ma Zhanshan in eastern Heilongjiang, launched an attack on Heihe at the same time. Li Haiqing's troops once attacked the Qiqihar Railway Station, but were forced to withdraw due to lack of supplies. The Japanese were caught off guard by Su Bingwen's rebellion. At this time, because the Japanese Consul Yamazaki and 100 Japanese residents in Manzhouli were all detained by Su, and because the area west of Heihe was vast and the troops were insufficient to be allocated, they did not dare to use heavy troops to suppress Su and others immediately. Instead, they sought to resolve the situation through political means. After the incident, Major Miyazaki of the Harbin Japanese Special Service Organ took a plane to Hailar and dropped a letter tube midway, hoping for a peaceful solution. The Volunteer Army ignored it. On the second day, Ji Handong's 2,000 troops of the 60th Route of the National Salvation Army recovered Suizhong and shot down two Japanese planes. They withdrew immediately due to lack of reinforcements. From the second to the third day, the National Salvation Army had repeated contacts with the Japanese army along the Nen River. Zhang Dianjiu's troops were completely concentrated in Fularji. In eastern Heilongjiang, the vanguard of the Volunteer Army reached Hulan River and contacted the Volunteer Army in Lihetun, Anda County. On the second day, the people of Hailar held a mass meeting in Asian Park, paraded, and the whole city went on strike for a day, presenting Su Bingwen with a banner that said "Fighting to the End." The people's feelings were exceptionally excited. At this time, Su's main force was concentrated in Boketu and Zhalan Nor, along the Middle East Road. One supply station was set up in Hailar, Mianduhe, Boketu, and Zhalantun. From Zhalantun in the east to Fularji, Zhang Dianjiu's troops were responsible for the defense. West of Ang'angxi, all belonged to the National Salvation Army's sphere of influence.

From the 21st to the 23rd, there were fierce battles in Fularji and Huerhula, and the volunteer armies appeared and disappeared in various places, with alternating victories and defeats. On the night of the 3rd, Li Haiqing's troops attacked the Ang'angxi station, and Pu Bingshan's troops advanced towards Yingtun, also gaining an advantage. However, the Volunteer Army lacked ammunition, and although their momentum was strong, they could not withstand the fierce artillery fire of the Japanese army. The Japanese army also often used planes to bomb the Volunteer Army's positions, so our side suffered considerable losses. On November 4, Chief of Staff Iso of the Japanese Army again proposed peace talks to Su Bingwen. Su proposed four conditions for a ceasefire: (1) The Japanese troops in Fularji would withdraw and be stationed by Su's troops; (2) Pay 300,000 yuan in back pay; (3) Manchukuo must "show sincerity"; (4) Not a single Japanese soldier may enter Hulunbuir. The Japanese side found these conditions difficult to accept, but the Japanese army believed that the peace talks were not yet hopeless. On the 10th, they sent negotiator Colonel Komatsubara by plane to Mazulef Kaya in Russian territory to request Su Bingwen to send a representative to negotiate peace terms. Su still refused. The Japanese army headquarters then decided to sacrifice the Japanese expatriates in Manzhouli and launch an attack. On the 19th, the enemy, covered by tanks, began to attack the Peng Hua Zhen position, and the puppet army also attacked from Linjia Dian. After three days of fierce fighting, the Volunteer Army fell one after another, with many casualties. Therefore, there were fierce battles in the Baiquan-Mingshui area for several days. The Ma army was still wearing unlined clothes, and they lacked both guns and ammunition. They constantly engaged in hand-to-hand combat, fighting in the snow and ice, with their hands and feet frozen. The Japanese army advanced with planes and tanks in large numbers. After three days and nights of bloody battles, the Ma army had to retreat to Tongbei. On the 12th, Su Bingwen, Ma Zhanshan, Ding Chao, Li Du, Wang Delin, Li Haiqing, and other anti-Japanese generals from the three provinces jointly sent a telegram to the League of Nations, first describing the process from September 18 to the forging of public opinion and the organization of the puppet state of Manchukuo, then describing the fact that the people fought a bloody battle with the Japanese army for a year, and the tragic situation of the Japanese army killing more than 50,000 innocent people. They solemnly declared that the people of the Northeast would only resist the brutal Japanese and would never surrender. Unless all 30 million of our people were killed, the puppet organization would never be allowed to exist, nor would any illegal rights and interests be recognized, nor could we abandon sovereignty and create a so-called co-management situation. No one in China dares to allow the division of our territory. Even if the government cannot recover the lost territory by force, the people will unite and vow to drive the Japanese invaders out of the country and restore our rivers and mountains. The Japanese were even more angry upon hearing this. The Japanese army immediately defeated the Ma army in the east and returned westward with their troops. At that time, the situation of the National Salvation Army was as follows: (1) The main force of Pu Bingshan's troops had moved to the vicinity of Nehe, and they had been counterattacking for days, with alternating victories and defeats. (2) Ma Jun's Xu Zicui brigade was stationed northeast of Ningnian. (3) Deng Wenda was in the Anda area and had occasional contact with the enemy. Li Haiqing's main force was in the Wangkui-Anda area. (4) The two troops of Cai Hongyou and Li Lingji were frequently active in the Hailun-Suihua-Hulan area on the Huhai Line. On the 27th, 28th, and 29th, the citizens' groups and commercial federations of 30 counties in Heilongjiang Province, and the Hulunbuir Mongolian banner, held a representative conference in Hailar, deciding on 17 articles of the anti-Japanese program, and unanimously vowed to resist Japan to the death. The people's morale was extremely high, but the National Salvation Army lacked supplies in the rear and had difficulty in combat. The Japanese army also specialized in bombing with planes. How could flesh and blood easily resist bombs? Now they can barely hold on, but what will happen in the future? I am afraid there is more pessimism and less optimism. (November 30)

Taking advantage of this tenth anniversary, I have invited all the elders to come here for a talk. I have been in charge of the navy and stationed in Qingdao for eight years. I was ordered to take concurrent charge of municipal administration last year, and it will soon be a year. The progress in repairing roads and running schools has been very rapid, which is a good phenomenon. Hunan Province Issues Paper Money to Purchase Grain

The Provincial Bank Issues 1.5 Million Yuan in Paper Money to Purchase Large Quantities of Rice for Transportation to Hankou for Sale, Establishing a Separate Sales and Transportation Agency with Completely Independent Accounting 58

Changsha Dispatch: The Hunan Provincial Bank was established with a capital of 2 million yuan allocated by Lu Diping when he governed Hunan. Initially, it did not issue paper money. It was not until last year that He Jian approved the issuance of fractional notes, divided into three denominations: 1 jiao, 2 jiao, and 5 jiao. Originally, only 500,000 yuan was issued, but it was subsequently increased twice, and now the total issuance has reached 1.5 million yuan. Because it is fully backed by cash reserves, its credit is considered sound. Now, the provincial government, considering that Hunan Province has had a bumper harvest this year, resulting in excessive stockpiling of grain with no one to transport and sell it, and that the rural economy and market finance have been greatly affected, has decided to have the bank issue an additional 1.5 million yuan in one-yuan paper money to be used for purchasing grain for transportation out of the province. A Grain Transportation and Sales Committee has also been established to oversee all matters. Yesterday, Zhao Heng, the president of the bank, submitted a proposal to the provincial government outlining the method for issuing additional paper money and transporting grain. The submission reads as follows: "In accordance with your order, this bank is investigating the proposal to issue an additional 1.5 million yuan in Hunan Provincial Bank notes to purchase grain for storage, which will be kept by the bank as collateral for the additional banknotes and will not be allocated or borrowed to maintain credit. In the meantime, the Grain Transportation and Sales Committee's letter states that market finance has been stagnant recently, and there has been no improvement in grain circulation. The committee resolved at its plenary meeting yesterday to sell 100,000 shi of grain purchased by your bank on a temporary basis, transport it to the creek in batches, store it in warehouses, and sell it at the appropriate time. If the price is acceptable and sales are somewhat active, please continue the transfer to avoid hoarding, etc. As it concerns the relief of the rural economy and the regulation of market finance, it is imperative to act without delay. A proposal for issuing additional banknotes and purchasing and transporting grain, along with the reasons, was submitted to the Bank Supervisory Committee for resolution. (A) The revised main points of the banknote printing method were passed as follows: (1) The name should only state the Hunan Provincial Bank. (2) The denomination is one yuan, and it should state that it is fully redeemable, with the total amount in accordance with the provincial government's instructions. (3) The location of the banknote printing will be determined by the head office. (4) The method for managing the reserve fund will be formulated separately by the head office and submitted to the meeting for public resolution. (B) The method for purchasing grain was passed in accordance with the method proposed by the head office, etc. Originally, the bank intended to solicit the consent of the Grain Transportation and Sales Committee and hire Luo Shendongyang as the director, and request that he find his own assistants, with all expenses to be reported and actually reimbursed, and the profits and losses not to be included in the bank's profits and losses. Subsequently, the Grain Transportation and Sales Committee added a letter urging Luo Shen to take the position, and then rented the house at No. 3 West Chang Street to establish an office, which began operations today. The bank has also issued a seal, with the inscription 'Seal of the Hunan Provincial Bank Grain Purchasing and Transportation Office,' and issued it to the office for use. The above is a summary of the handling situation submitted to your office for review and compliance." (December 9th)

Shantou

Public Security Bureau Auctions Smuggled Silver Ingots

No One Asks About the Auction Date, Shanghai Chaozhou Merchants Still Request Return 59

Shantou Dispatch: The Shantou Municipal Government issued an order in October prohibiting the export of silver cash in order to maintain market finance. However, most merchants only pursue their own private interests and continue to smuggle exports, causing a shortage of silver in the market and subsequently increasing daily interest rates and exchange rates. The municipal government, believing that merchants are incorrigible, ordered the Public Security Bureau to strictly enforce the ban. On the 17th of that month, 24 boxes of silver cash being transported to Shanghai were intercepted in a lighter on the sea. Except for seven boxes with customs supervision passports, the other seventeen boxes of silver ingots were immediately detained, and six silver smugglers were arrested. The criminals confessed to the Public Security Bureau that they had cast silver dollars into silver ingots. The Public Security Bureau then confiscated all of the silver ingots for use by the police training center and to purchase short guns. It is estimated that the seventeen boxes of silver are worth about 120,000 yuan. However, silver merchants were not convinced and submitted a petition to the higher authorities requesting their return, but it was not approved. Yesterday, the provincial government approved the Shantou Public Security Bureau to auction the silver. The bureau immediately announced that bidding would take place at the Municipal Chamber of Commerce on the 5th, and stipulated that the price of silver ingots would be calculated at 95% of the price of silver ingots within this ten-day period. Unexpectedly, no one went to vote on the afternoon of the 5th. It is said that the silver industry decided not to buy the silver. Miscellaneous merchants did not know the quality of the silver and did not dare to vote rashly. Moreover, they could not transport the silver to other ports for sale after buying it, so no one paid any attention to it. The Public Security Bureau has now rescheduled the vote for the 8th, and it is feared that no one will buy it at that time either. In addition, the Chaozhou Guild in Shanghai sent a telegram yesterday to the Eastern District Security Appeasement Commissioner's Office, the Chaozhou Customs Supervisor, and the Municipal Government, stating, "We have now received letters from Guanghua Zhuang, stating that seventeen boxes of silver ingots and six escorts who had been approved to be transported from Shantou to Shanghai in October were detained and announced to be confiscated and punished by the Shantou Public Security Bureau. The silver ingots were made by melting old silver utensils and are a type of cargo, so there is no discrepancy in allocating them for export. Please forward our request to return the people and goods." At the same time, we also received letters from Shanghai's Guanghua Zhuang agency, Puyi Zhuang, stating that the allocation and transportation of silver ingots were entrusted for collection and exchange, and the funds were prepaid. The detention of the silver ingots was unexpected. The end of the year is approaching, and finances are tight. If implicated, the impact will be significant. Please forward our request to the provincial Shantou authorities for verification and approval to return the silver ingots to the various Zhuang to avoid being implicated. Our guild believes that silver ingots are not prohibited items, so they should be allowed to be exported. Since the customs has approved their release, why does the Public Security Bureau overstep its authority and illegally announce confiscation and punishment, and detain people? This matter concerns merchants' capital and market finance. We urge you to investigate and promptly order the release of the seventeen boxes of silver ingots and six escorts detained by Guanghua Zhuang, etc., to alleviate merchants' difficulties and maintain commerce." It is unknown how this case will be resolved. (December 6th)

Held at the Hankou Chamber of Commerce, Yue's Coffin Shipped to Shaanxi for Burial 61

China Institute of Mining and Metallurgy

Please Maintain Jiaozuo Mining Rights 62

Oppose the Merger of the China and Fu Companies 63

The China Institute of Mining and Metallurgy submitted a petition to the National Government against the merger of the "China" and "Fu" coal mines in Jiaozuo, Henan Province, stating that the Fu Company in Jiaozuo, Henan Province, is a British-owned company registered in London, England. After the Sino-Japanese War in the late Qing Dynasty, the British took advantage of the Qing Dynasty's decline to obtain mining rights for coal mines in five counties bordering Henan and Shanxi. Later, the people of Shanxi opposed this and organized the Baojin Company to recover the shares and conduct mining on their own. The company then used the name of the Yu Feng Company to obtain mining rights for the Hanshan coal mine north of the Yellow River in Huaiqing Prefecture, declaring that the mines for which Yu Feng applied for mining rights could be transferred to the Fu Company. After the Boxer Rebellion, they used the name of the Fu Company to accept Yu Feng's mining rights. At that time, the people of Henan Province strongly opposed this, but to no avail. It was not until the beginning of the Republic of China that the landlords formed the Zhongzhou Company to compete with it. The company also protested to the government, but Yuan Shikai did not dare to offend foreigners. Therefore, the government acted as a mediator and ordered the merger of the Chinese companies to organize the Zhongyuan Company, which would use the Fu Company's method of separate mining and joint sales to eliminate competition. Until the May 30th Massacre in the Republic of China, the Fu Company's miners went on strike to support diplomacy. As a result, the Fu Company was closed down and has remained in a stalemate until now, unable to formally resume work. Recently, the Ministry of Industry and Commerce sent personnel to Henan to mediate and propose that the Zhongyuan Company be merged into the Fu Company, and that the Zhongyuan Company be valued at 5.05 million yuan and the Fu Company at 4.95 million yuan. The chairman of the board would be from the Zhongyuan Company and the vice chairman would be selected by the Fu Company. It was also said that the Fu Company had already agreed to this principle of joint investment. As soon as this proposal was made, the people of Bo'ai County rose up in opposition, and mining groups in various places also believed that the merger of "China" and "Fu" would undoubtedly give away Chinese mining rights and that the future was extremely dangerous. The institute, composed of miners from all over the country, believes that at this critical juncture concerning the life and death of our country's mining rights and the right to exchange currency, the heart is in danger, and we are unwilling to remain silent. There are various reasons why the "China" and "Fu" cannot be merged, which must be presented to your office.

(1) Coal mines are necessities for civilized peoples, the main fuel for modern industry, and must be managed by the state to prevent private monopolies and gradual autocracy and to avoid unequal distribution of wealth and social revolution. According to the late Premier Sun Yat-sen's instructions, all should be operated and managed by the state. Our country's iron mines were almost completely lost to the Japanese at the hands of past national traitors and treacherous merchants who were good at currying favor with foreigners. The Hanyeping Company is a precedent. In terms of coal mines, Fushun has fallen to Japan and Kailuan has been lost to Britain. Although the government has established sorting committees for the two mines, it has been difficult to reverse the situation due to the accumulated problems, and after several years, it has been unable to salvage the situation. With the overturned cart in front, how can we bear to repeat the same mistake? This is one reason why "China" and "Fu" should not be merged.

(2) In recent years, the Zhongyuan coal mine has made considerable profits due to the Fu Company's shutdown, and the Taihang Mountain area is densely populated. What people rely on for their livelihood is coal mining. Therefore, for thousands of years, they have been self-mining and self-selling, which is enough to support themselves. Since the Fu Company invaded the mining rights, the old civilian kilns have been forcibly occupied, and prices have been raised to speculate. The people's livelihood is almost cut off, and local order has been presented. Fortunately, the emergence of the Zhongyuan Company can still accommodate indigenous workers, the price of coal is reduced, and the people's difficulties are also relieved. At present, the annual coal sales in the area are more than enough to be supplied by the current Zhongyuan Company. If the two mines are merged and the production and capital are concentrated to the highest degree, the poor will become poorer and the rich will become richer. The local economic situation will be greatly affected, the people's livelihood will lose its basis, and the chaos will be difficult to clean up. This is the second reason why "China" and "Fu" should not be merged.

(3) If it is said that joint venture operation is a principle stipulated by the central government, and that foreigners are allowed to invest, it is also based on mining laws and regulations, and all Chinese people should abide by it. According to the late Premier Sun Yat-sen's teachings on using foreign capital, "If the right to develop is in our hands, we will survive, and if it is in the hands of others, we will perish." However, according to the contract signed between the Fu Company and the Yu Feng Company in the 24th year of Guangxu of the Qing Dynasty, "All scheduling of mining affairs and mining projects shall be handled jointly by the general manager of the company and the general manager of the Yu Feng Company. There shall also be one Chinese and one foreign director for each mining plant. The Chinese director shall handle negotiations and the inflow and outflow of money, the foreign director shall be the general manager, and the Chinese director shall audit the above clauses." From the perspective of the time, the Chinese directors did not have no power, but it did not take long for the darkness to be revealed. The name of the Yu Feng Company and the powers of the Chinese directors were completely reduced to nothing, and the mining industry was exclusively occupied by the Fu Company, causing problems that have not been solved to this day. With the rights in the hands of others, what is the use of regretting too late? Furthermore, Article 8 of the revised articles of association of the Zhongyuan Company's shareholders meeting in April of the Republic of China states that shares may not be transferred or mortgaged to non-Chinese. In the era of the previous warlord government, it was still stipulated that foreigners were not allowed to buy shares. Under the rule of the Kuomintang, it is truly incomprehensible to use this inferior strategy and give others a handle. The authorities are wise and will not do this. China, with its undeveloped geographical advantages, itself is limited by its financial resources. Therefore, it may need to rely on foreign capital to develop it. This does not mean that there is no need for joint ventures with foreigners. It must also be used by us. If this case is used as a condition for international exchanges and mutual assistance for friendship, there are still many industries in China that have not been developed that must be a joint venture, so there is no need to focus on the merger of the "China" and "Fu" mines and please the British. This is the third reason why "China" and "Fu" should not be merged.

(4) Our country's coal production reaches 25 million tons per year, of which the Fushun coal mine operated by Japan and the Kailuan coal mine controlled by the British produce nearly 14 million tons per year, which is more than half of the country's total output. The output of the two mines is rich and the consumption is light. Recently, the two mines have further reduced prices to compete for sales, and the country's coal industry will be unable to save itself. If the China and Fu companies are merged again, it will be like adding another formidable enemy to the country's coal industry. The trend will lead to a situation from which there is no recovery. Moreover, the British merchant Kaiping survived by merging with Luanzhou, and the Fu Company failed by leaving Zhongyuan. Merger benefits others, while non-merger benefits us. Its story is clear, and its reason is obvious. This is the fourth reason why "China" and "Fu" should not be merged.

(5) Article 8 of the revised articles of association of the Zhongyuan Company's shareholders meeting in October of the Republic of China states that shares may not be transferred, gifted, or mortgaged to non-Chinese. In the era of the previous Northern warlord government, it was still stipulated that foreigners were not allowed to buy shares. Even in the time when the evil Yuan Shikai was in power, the Zhongyuan Company, which was allowed to be jointly established by Chinese, and the Fu Company used separate mining and joint sales methods to eliminate competition. Now, this is merged and abolished. Under the rule of the Kuomintang, this kind of phenomenon is happening. How can we protect the foundation of the country? How can we gain the trust of the people? This is the fifth reason why "China" and "Fu" should not be merged. (6) Article 41 of the original contract of the Fu Company states, "If one party denies all or part of the clauses of this contract, this contract shall be invalid." The Fu Company has violated the contract and has not been able to fulfill it to this day. The people of Bo'ai County have already filed a complaint by telegram. In May of this year, Bai Da, the general manager of the Fu Company, admitted his mistake at the Henan Construction General Assembly in the presence of representatives of the people of Bo'ai. The fact that he could not fulfill the contract is obvious. The only plan for the present is to take advantage of the situation to declare this contract invalid in order to lift the shackles of unequal treaties for decades. Instead of coming up with this plan, the profitable Zhongyuan Company, which is run by ourselves, is forcibly merged into the Fu Company, which is used by the British as an instrument of aggression and violates the contract. It is really unknown what their intentions are. In the past, during the era of the joint sales of the Fu Zhong General Company, shareholders' profits were often less than one cent. Now, the Zhongyuan Company is able to distribute dividends of two fen three li. This is the effective result of not cooperating with the Fu Company. If we merge with it now, the profits will inevitably be deprived by the Fu Company by 50%. In terms of the effectiveness of the contract, there is only one way to cancel it. In terms of the interests of the shareholders, there is absolutely no need for a merger. This is the sixth reason why "China" and "Fu" should not be merged.

(7) The Fu Company has a deep grudge against the local area. This time, when it tried to start mining, the people of Bo'ai County gathered near the mining area without prior agreement, willing to fight to the death, tens of thousands or in groups. If it is necessary to have it resume work and co-operate with the Zhongyuan Company, although it will never cause a major incident. This is the seventh reason why "China" and "Fu" should not be merged.

Based on the above seven reasons, the reasons why "China" and "Fu" cannot be merged are very obvious. However, the authorities of the Ministry of Industry are unable to take this opportunity to free themselves from constraints, but are instead tempted by the sweet words of the Fu Company, ignoring the livelihoods of hundreds of thousands of people, advocating this sticky discussion of merger, in order to curry favor with foreigners. The people are panicked and do not know what to do. Reluctantly, we can only beg your office to comply with the sentiments of the people and promptly order the Executive Yuan to instruct the Ministry of Industry and Commerce to abolish the proposal to merge the "China" and "Fu" mines immediately in order to maintain public opinion and protect national rights.

Songjiang

Shanyang Farmers Resist Robbery and Die

Pu Meisheng, a resident of Maqiao Township, Shanyang, usually worked as a farmer for a living and was somewhat well-fed. Suddenly, at midnight on the 7th, seven or eight bandits came and smashed open the main door. His father, A Xiao, was awakened from his sleep, got up quickly with his clothes on, and tried to hold the door shut, but the bandits' brother was unstoppable and fired a gun. Unexpectedly, his father was shot in the lower body, blood flowed, and he died immediately. Seeing the disaster, the bandits dispersed in fright. Later, Wu Zhongxian, the town mayor, reported to the 16th District Office, which forwarded the report to the county government, which ordered the arrest. The Department of Education sent a commissioner to Songjiang to inspect.

The Provincial Department of Education Sent Investigators

The Provincial Department of Education sent Chief Compiler Yi Changzuo and Inspector Zhou to Songjiang to investigate the provincial middle schools and the educational administration and school education of various counties. Yesterday, they went to the provincial schools to inspect and investigate everything.

Commander Cao Inspects the Student Soldiers' Company

The former commander of the 2nd Security Regiment stationed in Songjiang, Cao

Pang, was ordered to lead his troops to Huining to suppress bandits, leaving the student soldiers' company stationed in Songjiang for training. The people of Songjiang, believing that the Jiangbei banditry had been quelled, had telegraphed the province requesting that Cao be transferred back to Songjiang, but to no avail. Now, Commander Cao took the opportunity to inspect the training results of the student soldiers' company in Songjiang this month. Leaders of various agencies specially held a banquet at the Chamber of Commerce to welcome him and strengthen ties.

Wuxi

Huazang Mountain Bay Reports Another Robbery

Huazang in the 17th District of the county

In the Shanwan area, at about 11:00 PM last night, six or seven bandits suddenly came to the home of resident Fan Lianfang, armed with sharp blades, electric batons, and other weapons. They spoke with a northern accent, broke down the door, and tied up Fan Lianfang first. Then, they separated and robbed for about two hours, looting ten yuan in cash, four sets of short shirts and trousers, 167 bean cakes, and five strong pigs, before roaring away. Afterwards, the 14th Branch of the Zhangshe Town Public Security Bureau in charge of the area seized a suspicious boat on the Mengwan River bank and arrested five suspects, Liang Dejin, Liang A'er, He Zhaoming, He Zhaoyu, and He Zhaoyou, all of whom denied the robbery. They were immediately sent to the County Public Security Bureau for interrogation.

The Jiangsu Provincial Government decided to abolish the Department of Industry. Yesterday, it telegraphed the national and provincial governments separately, requesting that the order be withdrawn to emphasize industry. Central officials are not the ones that a local government should change events. The industrial relations of the people of Su Province are under the jurisdiction of the construction hall, and the affairs are not specialized. This is not an intention to attach importance to the industry, and Director He has been in Su for many years and is familiar with the people's conditions. Zheng Lai government advocated slightly maintaining a line of vitality. This time, the Jiangsu province suddenly abolished the Industry Department, which is tantamount to announcing to the people of Su that all industries can be abandoned. It really makes the people of Su unable to escape death, wandering and pleading. Please be aware and correct it. The Su provincial government should immediately revoke the case of the abolition of the Industry Department, issue a clear order to revoke it, so as to avoid confusion and re-emphasize the industry. The Wuxi County Chamber of Commerce bows to the true desire to wait for orders to the extreme,

Jiangyin

Public Security Bureau Chief Accused of Thorough Investigation 64

Liu Hanzhen, the chief of the Public Security Bureau, has been in office for more than eight months. Due to lax management, incidents such as the expulsion of Li Mutang, the chief of the First Branch, by the police in the northern outskirts, and Zhou Fankai's, the patrol captain, affair with the female prisoner Feng Qimei, have occurred. Recently, citizens such as Zhang Xiaoyi have submitted a report to the Department of Civil Affairs, requesting the dismissal and punishment of the police due to such phenomena. After receiving the report, the Department of Civil Affairs approved the investigation and sent personnel to Jiangyin to conduct a secret investigation and report back for review.

Changshu

A Tragic Incident Arising from Business Competition 65

Celery is a type of agricultural product, and this county is a major producer of it, with annual exports of approximately two hundred thousand gold dollars. On the Shanghai side, the He Cheng Tong Ji Earth Products Firm, located at Lao Zha Bridge, has dispatched a dedicated representative to Changshu for procurement, resulting in exceptionally prosperous business. In addition to employing the resident director, Shi Haifu, they also employ seven or eight experienced clerks. Consequently, the majority of celery produced throughout the county is purchased by them. This lucrative situation has unfortunately led to a tragic and bloody incident. Since the He Cheng firm enjoys a monopoly on the local celery, other parties inevitably covet this business. However, due to the firm’s years of establishment, it has been difficult to break their hold. This autumn, a new firm, the Tong Tai Qia Ji Earth Products Firm, has also been established in Shanghai, near Lao Zha Bridge, and is attempting to compete with He Cheng. Since its opening, it has also sent representatives to Changshu to procure celery, but has not been as successful as He Cheng. As a result, there have been repeated conflicts between the employees of the two firms. Recently, Shi Haifu of He Cheng has been under pressure from the new firm, causing daily exports to plummet, averaging no more than twenty bundles per day. Consequently, the two sides have engaged in even more intense scheming and plotting. Until the other day, a brawl broke out. As a result, the new firm suffered losses. Yuan Shengzi and others went to the county to report their injuries. However, in retaliation, they immediately sent a telegram to Shanghai. Upon receiving the telegram, the Tong Tai firm, seeing that they were at a disadvantage, decided that a radical solution was necessary. They then invited Zhu Chang of the Axe Gang, intending to kill Shi Haifu of the old firm and others. On the morning of the ninth, sure enough, Axe Gang leader Lu Genlin led twenty or thirty followers, taking the Shun Li steamer to Changshu, stopping near Fan Jia Du, Xiaodongmen. They then searched in various directions, but bystanders were unaware of their purpose. Around eleven o'clock, before lunch, they learned that Shi Haifu was at the Qing Sheng Teahouse, and went there immediately. However, they were unable to find him. So they swarmed to the Tian Pan (where celery is processed) next to the Five Old Peaks, and saw the clerk Zhou Erbao, who was sorting celery. The Axe Gang members immediately rushed forward and hacked at Zhou. As a result, he received three axe wounds to the back, one to the right thigh, one to the armpit, and one to the left foot. Zhou immediately fainted and fell to the ground. Seeing that their plan had succeeded, the gang members dispersed. Li Sanzi and others, who were nearby, saw what happened and immediately reported it to Shi Haifu. Shi then entrusted someone to take the injured man to the Second Branch of the Public Security Bureau, report the incident, and request the apprehension of the Axe Gang. The branch police then sent Zhou Erbao to Jishan Hospital for treatment. Meanwhile, because such a tragic incident was unprecedented in Changshu, it is said that Officer Song issued an order dispatching police to search for the gang and impounding the Shun Li steamer, detaining its captain, Gong Chuangen. When questioned, Gong claimed to be a roughneck operating in Shanghai, and that he had been hired by Lu Genlin to come to Changshu, and was unaware of any killing plot. However, there were pistols and axes on the boat, and he was afraid of being harmed, so he did not report it. Subsequently, the police arrested gang leader Lu Genlin and followers Xu Yinhai, Yan Daxing, Zhang Zhiqin, and four others. At seven o'clock in the evening, they were escorted to the Public Security Bureau, where they were interrogated by the head of the judicial section. Lu and the others only admitted that Lu Genlin was the leader of the Axe Gang, 34 years old, living on Bansongyuan Road, Shanghai. They claimed that they had come to Changshu to investigate the celery gang's fight, and had not assaulted anyone, fearing that they were using a "bitter meat" trap. They claimed that since they were members of the Axe Gang, they would take responsibility for their own actions, and there was no need to deny it. The other statements were similar to the above. That night, the bureau detained all those involved. The next day (the 10th), they were handed over to the county government. However, on the night of the incident, rumors spread that more than twenty members of the Axe Gang had arrived on a Kunshan steamer and were hiding in the Xiayou East Monk Temple. Upon receiving the report, the Public Security Bureau immediately dispatched a large force to search, but found nothing. However, to prevent any unforeseen circumstances, the authorities imposed a curfew and conducted overnight searches of all hotels, especially in the Five Old Peaks and Fan Jia Shi, deploying more patrols. Fortunately, nothing happened overnight. As for Zhou Erbao, who was injured in the attack, he is currently 44 years old. After being sent to the hospital, Dr. Huang examined him and found that the axe wound to the armpit was the most dangerous, while the others were not life-threatening. However, due to excessive bleeding, there may be complications. Zhou regained consciousness around 3 or 4 pm and was able to speak. He said that he had a 76-year-old mother, wife, daughter and several other family members, and that he earned 18 yuan a month, which the family relied on for their livelihood.

Taicang

Robbery at Daopeng Temple Outside the South Gate 66

At around ten o'clock last night, the home of Xue Buzhou at Daopeng Temple outside the South Gate was suddenly invaded by more than ten bandits speaking with a foreign accent, wearing felt hats and galoshes. They first fired a shot and then broke through the side door and entered. Xue Buzhou and his wife, hearing the alarm, quickly hid in the pigsty, escaping harm. His elder brother, Xue Quan, was unable to escape in time and was tied up and tortured by the bandits. They robbed him of clothing and more than four hundred silver dollars, and after searching for an hour, they left with a whoop.

Nantong

Five Notorious Bandits Executed by Firing Squad in Tongru 67

The notorious bandits Feng Ziyun, Chen Heshang, Pan Changtai, Feng Le, and Jin Hongxu, who operated within the borders of Tongru, were successively captured by the police and local militia, and handed over to the county government. They all confessed to jointly using firearms to rob the homes of Xu Lianfen, Hua Jintai, and others, obtaining stolen goods, fatally wounding the victims, and resisting and killing members of the local defense force. They were sentenced to death. On the 10th, the provincial government approved the sentence by telegram. At noon, the five bandits were taken to Yaogang Road and executed by firing squad.

The Poison of Red Pills Spreads Deeper in Jiangbei 68

In Jiangbei's Tongru, Hai'an, and Taixing counties, the sale of red pills is flourishing. Young men and women are particularly fond of them. They are sold openly in the market, ninety pills for one yuan. The Chao Xin Company, which specializes in opium sales, is also affected by the influx of red pills, and its opium sales have declined.

Yangzhou

People of Mengcheng Form a Group to Come to Yangzhou 69

At ten o'clock on the morning of the tenth, eighty or ninety famine victims from Mengcheng County arrived outside the North Gate, and twenty of them had already gone to Beilai Temple to rest. The county government telephoned the Public Security Bureau to find a way to stop them. The bureau then instructed the Fourth Branch of the Public Security Bureau to instruct the police chief and police officers of the Bianyimen Outpost to expel them from the city.

Taixian

Suicide Due to Assault from Demanding Debt 70

Xu Houde, who sells cakes for a living in the thirteenth district of the county, Xu Xishe, has always been honest and timid. A few days ago, he demanded a debt from his cousin Xu Houxiang, but failed and was severely beaten. Feeling wronged and unable to seek redress, he committed suicide by taking poison. His wife, Ms. Tu, filed a complaint with the county government. After opening the coffin for inspection, it was found that he had injuries on both ribs and a swollen abdomen. It was determined that he had died from being beaten and taking poison. It is reported that the defendant has been taken to the county for questioning.

Page 10

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce Held a Memorial Service Yesterday for Four Martyred Boy Scouts

And the Memorial Monument Unveiling Ceremony

Attended by More Than Two Thousand Chinese and Foreign Guests

Chairman Chiang Gave an Honorary Medal on Behalf

Family Representative Mao Zhixiang Thanked

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce Boy Scouts Luo Yunxiang and other four martyrs sacrificed their lives in the January 28th Incident. Yesterday afternoon at 2:00 pm, a memorial service was held. Chiang Kai-shek, President of the Boy Scouts of China, presented the four martyred Boy Scouts with honorary awards, and the unveiling ceremony of the memorial monument was held. The venue was maintained by the Boy Scouts, postal workers, and Guangyi teams. Those in attendance included Chiang Kai-shek's representative, Teng Jie, General Director of the Boy Scouts of China; Xu Guanyu, representative of Zhu Jiahua, Director of the General Assembly; Jiang Wushi from the General Assembly Preparatory Office; Tong Hangbai of the Shanghai Council; Xu Peihuang, representative of Mayor Wu Tiecheng; Tu Xiaolai, Wang Yansong, Fang Jiaobo, Chen Songyuan, and Ye Jiaxing, Committee Members of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce; Zhang Xiang, representative of Garrison Commander Dai Ji; Zhu Jiaxiang of the Municipal Party Headquarters; Wang Zongjian, Superintendent of the Jianghai Customs; Hou Dachun, representative of Yang Hu, Director of the Security Department; Wang Xun of the Local Court; Sun Huiyu of the Second Branch of the High Court; Li Mengnan of the General Labor Union; Gong Xikui of the Public Security Bureau; Chen Baohua of the Social Affairs Bureau; Jiang Zhihua of the Public Works Bureau; Xu Xingjia of the Health Bureau; Yuan Fang of the Finance Bureau; Lin Kanghou of the Bankers' Association; various industry associations, labor unions, schools, farmers' associations, and others; Gamperlin Changxun, Qiu Siden, Bairoson, and Gelinbo from the Shanghai Western Boy Scout Branch; Boy Scouts from a total of 129 troops, including Troops 221, 678, 604, 550, 268, 178, 213, 230, 679, 113, 510, 349, 383, 352, 250, 677, 179, the YMCA, Guang Gong, Jin Rong, and other entire Boy Scout organizations, totaling approximately 2,000 people.

Medal Presentation Ceremony 71

At 2:00 pm, the meeting was announced to be in session. After the music was played, Chairman Xu Zicheng reported that "During the January 28th Incident, the 50th Troop organized a battlefield rescue team. Unfortunately, the four martyrs Luo Yunxiang and others went missing. Although we tried our best, we were ultimately disappointed. We are holding a memorial service today, but we still cannot see the loyalty of the four martyrs. Therefore, Chairman Chiang Kai-shek of the Central General Association specially presented honorary medals, but this still cannot express the bravery of the four martyrs. Therefore, the Municipal Chamber of Commerce is building a memorial tablet." Then, General Assembly representative Teng Jie presented the honorary medals and delivered a speech, and Ye Chunnian, the head of the 50th Troop, led the music without playing it. (Photo by Li Zunyong of the Memorial Service for the Four Boy Scout Martyrs of Songhu)

Chairman's Speech 72

General Assembly representative Teng Jie delivered a speech, saying, "Chairman, distinguished guests, Boy Scout comrades, today the Shanghai Boy Scout Council is holding a memorial service here for the four Boy Scout martyrs of Songhu. President Chiang Kai-shek of the Boy Scout General Assembly is unable to attend in person due to busy government affairs, so he has specially sent his brother to represent him and posthumously award honorary medals. In this great and solemn ceremony, in addition to representing the President in expressing great respect, one's heart is filled with infinite grief and emotion. We recall the past revolutions and the memorial services held to commemorate the martyrs who sacrificed themselves for the cause and for the nation, and we have held them countless times. But in the Boy Scout movement, the sacrifices made in this way can be counted as the first. It is not only the first time for Chinese Boy Scouts, but also probably the first time for Boy Scouts in the world. So this must be considered the most tragic and glorious page in our Boy Scout history. We know that during the European War, Boy Scouts from various countries, in order to fulfill their mission of rescuing people, helping others, and promoting world peace, did not hesitate to sacrifice everything to help the disaster victims in the war zones, maintain traffic in the war zones, and treat the wounded and killed soldiers. In four years, we have never heard of Boy Scouts wearing official Boy Scout uniforms and wearing the Red Cross symbol, which prohibits hatred, being brutally murdered. This time, in order to develop its continental policy ambitions and fulfill its dream of unifying the world, Japan invaded our Northeast, which was not enough, and then attacked our Shanghai. The January 28th War destroyed Zhabei, the economic center of our country, and slaughtered countless innocent people. At that time, the 50th Troop, driven by the mission of the Boy Scouts, worked tirelessly and fearlessly, running around and shouting amidst the bombing of airplanes and the shooting of artillery, completely dedicated to rescuing disaster victims and the wounded. At that time, they were not only wearing Boy Scout uniforms, but also wearing the Red Cross symbol. I never thought that the barbaric Japanese would falsely accuse them of being spies and use cruel means to secretly arrest them, destroy their bodies, and eliminate all traces. Our four brave Boy Scouts sacrificed their lives as a result. We know that our Boy Scouts are dedicated to maintaining world peace and dedicated to upholding justice and humanity. Anyone who opposes Boy Scouts, hates Boy Scouts, and harms Boy Scouts is trying to undermine world peace and violate justice and humanity. This kind of person is the common enemy of our Boy Scouts, the common enemy of Boy Scouts all over the world, and the common enemy of all mankind. For the sake of seeking world peace and upholding justice and humanity, we Boy Scouts should appeal to Boy Scouts all over the world and appeal to all mankind to rise up and overthrow this common enemy of mankind. This time, the struggle of our 50th Troop was to fight for justice, humanity, and world peace. The sacrifice of the four Boy Scouts was also a sacrifice for justice, humanity, and world peace. This kind of struggle and sacrifice has infinite value and infinite glory. Therefore, our un-dead 50th Troop Boy Scouts and the un-dead national Boy Scouts, in addition to passive commemoration, must actively continue their spirit to prepare to overthrow the world's common enemy. That is, our 50th Troop must continue this spirit, and the national Boy Scouts must follow the spirit of the 50th Troop in this struggle and sacrifice. Only in this way can we hope for the revival of our national spirit, and can we hope for the realization of world peace. Only then can we be worthy of the significance of holding this memorial service today."

Memorial Service 73

After the medal presentation ceremony, the memorial service was held. After the elegy was played, Chairman Tong Hangbai led everyone in paying their highest respects to the martyred heroes and delivered a eulogy, saying, "Today is the memorial service for the four martyred heroes. We are not just holding this memorial service and ending it. Boy Scouts serve the community and rescue people on the battlefield, and unfortunately sacrificed their own lives. This spirit is valuable. I hope that the people of our country will embrace this spirit to recover the lost territory of the Northeast. The four heroes sacrificed themselves for the country, and they have fulfilled their responsibilities as citizens. I know that the four heroes all served in the business community, and that they engaged in Boy Scout training and served the community in their spare time. This is admirable." After the flower offering, Wu Letian read the eulogy, and General Assembly representative Teng Jie, General Assembly Director representative Xu Guanyu, Chinese Red Cross representative Ji Heqin, Municipal Chamber of Commerce representative Wang Xiaolai, Boy Scout Council Director Wang Gang, and others led all the Boy Scouts. Mayor representative Xu Peihuang, Garrison Commander representative Zhang Xiang, Municipal Party Headquarters representative Zhu Jiaxiang, and others successively offered sacrifices. After the speeches, Mao Zhixiang, the representative of the families of the four martyrs, delivered a thank-you speech, saying, "Luo Yunxiang and others sacrificed their lives for the public good. We are grateful to the Chamber of Commerce and the Red Cross for their condolences, to the President for awarding honorary medals, to all sectors of society for their memorial services, and to the Chamber of Commerce for building a memorial monument. Although they are dead, they are still honored." Finally, the elegy was played.
